# Cause optional modules to be loaded above generic modules
install snd /sbin/modprobe --ignore-install snd $CMDLINE_OPTS && { /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-ioctl32 ; /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-seq ; }
#
# Workaround at bug #499695 (reverted in Ubuntu see LP #319505)
install snd-pcm /sbin/modprobe --ignore-install snd-pcm $CMDLINE_OPTS && { /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-pcm-oss ; : ; }
install snd-mixer /sbin/modprobe --ignore-install snd-mixer $CMDLINE_OPTS && { /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-mixer-oss ; : ; }
install snd-seq /sbin/modprobe --ignore-install snd-seq $CMDLINE_OPTS && { /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-seq-midi ; /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-seq-oss ; : ; }

install snd-via82xx /sbin/modprobe --ignore-install snd-via82xx $CMDLINE_OPTS && { /sbin/modprobe --quiet --use-blacklist snd-seq ; }

# Additional settings - these settings can improve the network
# security of the host and prevent against some network attacks
# including spoofing attacks and man in the middle attacks through
# redirection. Some network environments, however, require that these
# settings are disabled so review and enable them as needed.
#
# Ignore ICMP broadcasts
#net.ipv4.icmp_echo_ignore_broadcasts = 1
#
# Ignore bogus ICMP errors
#net.ipv4.icmp_ignore_bogus_error_responses = 1

# _or_
# Accept ICMP redirects only for gateways listed in our default
# gateway list (enabled by default)
# net.ipv4.conf.all.secure_redirects = 1
#
# Do not send ICMP redirects (we are not a router)
#net.ipv4.conf.all.send_redirects = 0
#
# Do not accept IP source route packets (we are not a router)
#net.ipv4.conf.all.accept_source_route = 0
#net.ipv6.conf.all.accept_source_route = 0
#
# Log Martian Packets
#net.ipv4.conf.all.log_martians = 1

# the following stops low-level messages on console
kernel.printk = 4 4 1 7
# Protect the zero page of memory from userspace mmap to prevent kernel
# NULL-dereference attacks against potential future kernel security
# vulnerabilities.  (Added in kernel 2.6.23.)
#
# While this default is built into the Ubuntu kernel, there is no way to
# restore the kernel default if the value is changed during runtime; for
# example via package removal (e.g. wine, dosemu).  Therefore, this value
# is reset to the secure default each time the sysctl values are loaded.
vm.mmap_min_addr = 65536

# Turn on Source Address Verification in all interfaces to
# prevent some spoofing attacks.
net.ipv4.conf.default.rp_filter=1
net.ipv4.conf.all.rp_filter=1

# Turn on SYN-flood protections.  Starting with 2.6.26, there is no loss
# of TCP functionality/features under normal conditions.  When flood
# protections kick in under high unanswered-SYN load, the system
# should remain more stable, with a trade off of some loss of TCP
# functionality/features (e.g. TCP Window scaling).
net.ipv4.tcp_syncookies=1

### Post by dino99 on 2010-07-15

### Post by simosx on 2010-07-15
What's needed is to run 'alsa-info.sh' and report the URL that it produces with the audio card info.

Per the Ubuntu Sound Troubleshooting Wiki, run

wget -O alsa-info.sh [http://alsa-project.org/alsa-info.sh](http://alsa-project.org/alsa-info.sh) && bash ./alsa-info.sh

and select Y when it asks you to send the sound card details to the [www.alsa-project.org](www.alsa-project.org) website. It will then tell you the URL with the details; paste the URL here.

---

### Post by buvesz on 2010-07-15

### Post by simosx on 2010-07-15
> **buvesz said:**
> Ok. Here is the link

[http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=668c75d4245a319107cd92aa1c2c9449f57a6d77](http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=668c75d4245a319107cd92aa1c2c9449f57a6d77)

Anyone knows what might be going on ?

The alsa-info.sh output shows that your sound card is not identified by the linux kernel (ALSA subcomponent).

The search string for more information is *ATI IXP SB4x0 ALSA*.

From the search, follow the advice at
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9383311&postcount=30](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9383311&postcount=30)

If you notice, the guy at the above discussion managed to find the correct parameters. I think he forgot to write them so you may have to pm them.

In any case, the proper solution is, once you find the correct manual parameters, to inform the ALSA developers so that in newer versions of the Linux kernel your card is autodetected.
Google searching shows that the specific card has been out since 2008 and it's sad that in 2010 users cannot have it autodetected.

---

### Post by buvesz on 2010-07-17

From the search, follow the advice at

If you notice, the guy at the above discussion managed to find the correct parameters. I think he forgot to write them so you may have to pm them.

In any case, the proper solution is, once you find the correct manual parameters, to inform the ALSA developers so that in newer versions of the Linux kernel your card is autodetected.
Google searching shows that the specific card has been out since 2008 and it's sad that in 2010 users cannot have it autodetected.

### Post by lidex on 2010-07-18
You'll need to get as current as possible with your drivers. If you have alsa-backports installed, please remove it. Then use the alsa-upgrade link in my sig to update.
The link referenced by *simosx* boils down to this. Using a Terminal="Applications->Accessories->Terminal"
Open this file for editing:
```
 gksudo gedit /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base.conf 
```
Insert this line at the bottom:
```
 options snd-hda-intel model=oqo 
```
Save. Close. Reboot. Check your levels in alsamixer.
```
 alsamixer 
```
Press <F6> to select the correct soundcard.
Press <F3> to show playback levels. <F4> selects capture levels [or use <Tab>]
Use the left/right arrow keys to select and up/down arrow keys to change levels. <M> to mute/unmute.
Go to "System ->Preferences ->Sound" and make sure the correct soundcard is default and adjust your profile on the hardware tab.

---

Re-install alsa:
Using a Terminal="Applications->Accessories->Terminal"
```
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get upgrade
```
```
sudo apt-get purge linux-sound-base alsa-base alsa-utils

```
```
sudo apt-get install linux-sound-base alsa-base alsa-utils gdm ubuntu-desktop

```
**gdm and ubuntu-desktop usually get taken out in the process, so we add them back**
**Reboot.**

### Post by simosx on 2010-07-20
> **chudder said:**
> Unfortunately, probably a related issue, anything that has to do with OSS4 doesn't install correctly.  What could be going on there?  I'm going to continue with the steps you gave me.

Thanks

Okay, now I'm rebooting, I'll let you know what happens

Installing OSS4 is a bit messy and is what we call unsupported (that is, it is not part of the Ubuntu packages and does not receive as much testing as Alsa). As already noted, here the Alsa kernel module is not loaded. Compared to OSS4, Alsa is part of the mainline Linux kernel and receives tremendous testing.

What I recommend for you is 
1. to clean up your system (most probably reinstall)
2. apply all updates that are available
3. Use 'alsa-info.sh' to retrieve your sound card details. Keep the URL safe and post here.
4. Test sound and write down what works, what does not work.
5. If there are things that do not work, then use the AlsaUpgrade script (see this forum) to upgrade fully to the latest version of Alsa. Once you do this (and reboot), try Alsa-info.sh again and post here the updated sound card details.

For the majority of the cases, your sound should work fine. If it still does not work, then you need to tinker the Alsa kernel module parameters in /etc. If you do this and you make it work, then it's possible to write (with the forum's help) a small patch for the Linux kernel so that your sound card is autodetected. See example at 
[http://simos.info/blog/archives/984](http://simos.info/blog/archives/984)

I think this is the best practice on sound issues.

The digital output is the HDMI output of your laptop.
In your alsa-info.sh file I can see some warnings/errors at the end of the report.
In addition, you are using the stock Alsa that comes with Ubuntu 10.04. It is possible that sound has improved in the latest Alsa, 1.0.23.
So, what you should do in your case is install the latest Alsa. 

To update to the latest Alsa, follow the instructions for AlsaUpgrade,
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6589810#post6589810](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6589810#post6589810)
Once you do this, reboot your computer and create a fresh alsa-info.sh.
Hopefully your microphone will be working.

HDMI might be working already, try to google for 'HDMI Ubuntu' or 'HDMI Pulseaudio'. With Alsa 1.0.23 you will be certain what's going on.

(Update: Your alsa-info.sh mentions that your sound chipset is 'CX20582'. If you google 'CX20582 Ubuntu', you will find several results. In one, they verify that there are problems with Ubuntu 10.04, so you need to upgrade Alsa anyway.)

The commands may look a bit cryptic. The part that goes wrong is the one where you download this AlsaUpgrade-1.0.23-2.tar.
What you did not do is click on the link that says *AlsaUpgrade-1.0.23-2.tar  (30.0 KB, 4221 views)*. When you click there, then Firefox will download the package and place it (by default) in the Downloads subdirectory. Then, the subsequence commands should work.
Give this a try again.

lkjoel gives some new instructions. Those instructions perform the downloading using the command line tool, thus you do not need to click and download with Firefox. So, try the original instructions where you download with Firefox, and if that fails, you can perform the download using the following command (in command line):

wget "http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=156468&d=1273598001" -O AlsaUpgrade-1.0.23-2.tar

(the above command is a replacement for the downloading of the file with Firefox. The rest of the command still apply.)

Note that these commands may take some time to compile the latest version of Alsa. Quite a few Ubuntu software development will be downloaded, but the process should be fully automated.

### Post by lidex on 2010-07-21
> **newleaf said:**
> Thank you.  I was able to complete all of the Alsa upgrade steps.  Here is my new link: [http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=5d11c5be5e6b5944f0d254619ae3c87c6bfbae9d](http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=5d11c5be5e6b5944f0d254619ae3c87c6bfbae9d)

Now there are more hardware options on Sound Preferences, but still the only one that works is analog.  Also, when I plug in headphones, the laptop speakers play at the same time.  The external mic on my headset does work.

This is interesting... when I try to record and play back a sound in Sound Recorder, it acts like it is recording (the levels indicator moves, unlike before), but when I playback it gives this error:  "GStreamer error: state change failed and some element failed to post a proper error message with the reason for the failure."
Using a Terminal="Applications->Accessories->Terminal"
Open this file for editing:
```
 gksudo gedit /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base.conf 
```
Insert these lines at the bottom:
```
options snd-hda-intel model=laptop
options snd-hda-intel position_fix=1 enable=yes
 
```
Save. Close. Reboot. Check your levels in alsamixer.
```
 alsamixer 
```
Press <F6> to select the correct soundcard.
Press <F3> to show playback levels. <F4> selects capture levels [or use <Tab>]
Use the left/right arrow keys to select and up/down arrow keys to change levels. <M> to mute/unmute.
Go to "System ->Preferences ->Sound" and make sure the correct soundcard is default and adjust your profile on the hardware tab.

---

### Post by simosx on 2010-07-22
> **newleaf said:**
> Thank you.  I was able to complete all of the Alsa upgrade steps.  Here is my new link: [http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=5d11c5be5e6b5944f0d254619ae3c87c6bfbae9d](http://www.alsa-project.org/db/?f=5d11c5be5e6b5944f0d254619ae3c87c6bfbae9d)

Now there are more hardware options on Sound Preferences, but still the only one that works is analog.  Also, when I plug in headphones, the laptop speakers play at the same time.  The external mic on my headset does work.

This is interesting... when I try to record and play back a sound in Sound Recorder, it acts like it is recording (the levels indicator moves, unlike before), but when I playback it gives this error:  "GStreamer error: state change failed and some element failed to post a proper error message with the reason for the failure."

Reading through your newest alsa-info.sh, we learn the updated codec name,
[INDENT]
Codec: Conexant CX20582 (Pebble)[/INDENT]

At this stage, we get more information if we google for "Conexant CX20582 alsa". From the results we can see that there are people that managed to get sound working.

Before going to technical details, could you please verify that in the Sound Preferences you have
1. Five tabs, with titles 'Sound Effects', 'Hardware', 'Input', 'Output' and 'Applications'.
2. Under each of 'Input' and 'Output' you have the option to manually select the input and output devices. Normally you do not need to configure those, as they are autodetected (if you put a headphone, the speakers should go mute and you hear from the headphone).
According to your alsa-info.sh, you should have one input (your analog microphone) and at most three outputs (analog output for speakers, possibly digital output if your motherboard does have an SPIDF connector, and your HDMI output).
For the case of HDMI output (which is a type of digital output), I do not know if the motherboard can autodetect when you connect the cable. You may have to manually select HDMI from the list.
3. The message "GStreamer error: state change failed and some element failed to post a proper error message with the reason for the failure." is something I did not find much about. It could be an issue that was just triggered because something is missing from the sound configuration.

Have a go with the above; what I believe is needed to get the microphone hotplugging to work, is to modify the Alsa source code in a similar way to 
[http://kerneltrap.org/mailarchive/git-commits-head/2010/5/5/32500](http://kerneltrap.org/mailarchive/git-commits-head/2010/5/5/32500)
(we would just need to add the line that starts with the plus sign ('+')).
When you are ready, ask for instructions on this.

Your new alsa-info.sh output has the 'snd-hda-intel: model=acer' setting.

### Post by joejk2 on 2010-07-23
> **lidex said:**
> Using a Terminal="Applications->Accessories->Terminal"
Open this file for editing:
```
 gksudo gedit /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base.conf 
```
Insert these lines at the bottom:
```
options snd-hda-intel model=laptop
options snd-hda-intel position_fix=1 enable=yes
 
```
Save. Close. Reboot. Check your levels in alsamixer.
```
 alsamixer 
```
Press <F6> to select the correct soundcard.
Press <F3> to show playback levels. <F4> selects capture levels [or use <Tab>]
Use the left/right arrow keys to select and up/down arrow keys to change levels. <M> to mute/unmute.
Go to "System ->Preferences ->Sound" and make sure the correct soundcard is default and adjust your profile on the hardware tab.


As well as making these modifications, try also purging pulseaudio: 
```

sudo apt-get purge pulseaudio

```

Pulseaudio has been the root of my problems over several upgrades...

**EDIT:** This fix proved temporary.  After 2.5 years of hacking sound, I followed the above advice of Simosx, and made a clean install of 10.04.  *Everything* works now; even the in-built microphone!

---

### Post by simosx on 2010-07-23
> **joejk2 said:**
> As well as making these modifications, try also purging pulseaudio: 
```

sudo apt-get purge pulseaudio

```

Pulseaudio has been the root of my problems over several upgrades...

If someone makes such drastic changes like removing PulseAudio or installing OSS4, I find it important to mention it in every reply when asking help. These suggestions are quite drastic and can mess up an installation. 

There has been lots of abuse on PulseAudio where people put the blame there instead of investigating deeper and understanding what's going on. PulseAudio is an amazing piece of software which makes Linux a usable home computer. Most of the issues with sound on Linux have to do with minor changes in the chipsets where we need to inform Alsa of these changes and sound works fine. Reading the output of alsa-info.sh we are able to get a good picture on what Alsa is doing irrespective of the PulseAudio layer. If the Alsa layer looks good, then we continue to investigate in the PulseAudio layer. 

Does your Skype not work well with PulseAudio? Try to get the Sound Recorder to record and playback your voice. If Sound Recorder can do this, then Skype is to blame.

Does your obscure SDL-based game fail in audio? Many old closed-source programs do not understand pulseaudio. You may be able to get around it with padsp or similar commands. These games need update.

---

### Post by newleaf on 2010-07-28

To answer Simosx:

> **simosx said:**
> Reading through your newest alsa-info.sh, we learn the updated codec name,[INDENT]
Codec: Conexant CX20582 (Pebble)[/INDENT]At this stage, we get more information if we google for "Conexant CX20582 alsa". From the results we can see that there are people that managed to get sound working.

Before going to technical details, could you please verify that in the Sound Preferences you have
1. Five tabs, with titles 'Sound Effects', 'Hardware', 'Input', 'Output' and 'Applications'.
2. Under each of 'Input' and 'Output' you have the option to manually select the input and output devices. Normally you do not need to configure those, as they are autodetected (if you put a headphone, the speakers should go mute and you hear from the headphone).
According to your alsa-info.sh, you should have one input (your analog microphone) and at most three outputs (analog output for speakers, possibly digital output if your motherboard does have an SPIDF connector, and your HDMI output).
For the case of HDMI output (which is a type of digital output), I do not know if the motherboard can autodetect when you connect the cable. You may have to manually select HDMI from the list.
3. The message "GStreamer error: state change failed and some element failed to post a proper error message with the reason for the failure." is something I did not find much about. It could be an issue that was just triggered because something is missing from the sound configuration.

Have a go with the above; what I believe is needed to get the microphone hotplugging to work, is to modify the Alsa source code in a similar way to 
[http://kerneltrap.org/mailarchive/git-commits-head/2010/5/5/32500](http://kerneltrap.org/mailarchive/git-commits-head/2010/5/5/32500)
(we would just need to add the line that starts with the plus sign ('+')).
When you are ready, ask for instructions on this.

### Post by simosx on 2010-08-04
> **newleaf said:**
> 
...
The microphone on my headphones works now, but laptop speakers do not mute when I have the headphones plugged in.  Sound Recorder works, as do all of the other sound applications, (as long as sound preferences are set to analog duplex), but sound in Skype, both input and output, does not work.

Edit:  After I posted this, I lost all sound again.  It happened right after I tried to use Skype.  Frustrating.

It is possible that Skype is messing with the audio system and caused PulseAudio to crash. For example, Alsa may not work too well with your sound card so if Skype is too intensive, it may crash the PulseAudio server. In addition, check the Skype Audio settings; it should be all set to PulseAudio (otherwise Skype may try to connect directly to the sound card and block other access).

What you need to do is reboot and try again.
If sound messes up again, then create a new alsa-info.sh information file and post here. The 'dmesg' section of the file should report if there are any kernel warnings/errors relating to sound.

If the speakers do not mute when you plug the headset, then this is something that Alsa needs to fix. We can report to the alsa-devel mailing list so they can fix it.

---

### Post by andreseso on 2012-08-22
With the installation of Precise I found out that I did not have any sound. I do not know how I found out that the kernel module for my soundcard was not loaded at boot time. I got sound executing **sudo modprobe snd-hda-intel** Some weeks later I did ** grep  -nri snd-hda-intel /etc/modprobe.d/***

I was able to get sound executing **sudo vim /etc/modprobe.d/oss4-base_noALSA.conf** Yestrday I did **sudo aptitude remove oss4-dkms** to keep my Precise from complaining
